794	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">BSMMU and others Vs. Dr. Zahidul Haq</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO. 3832 OF 2017.  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Hasan Foez Siddique, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on- Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ (AD) </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University represented by its Vice Chancellor and others</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Dr. Zahidul Haq </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Words and Phrases </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"> </p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 104.9pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top" width="140"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/Downloads/Issue__September__2019(2)/Issue__September_19__C.%20P.%203832%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___1_.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 93.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University represented by its Vice Chancellor and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ve<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">rsus</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Dr. Zahidul Haq</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">...Respondent<u></u></span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 12.0pt .85pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Words and Phrases </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Experience </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Experience means a state, extent, or duration of being engaged in a particular </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">study or work. A word implying skill, facility,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> or practical wisdom gained by personal knowledge, feeling, and action, and also the course or process by which one attains </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">knowledge or wisdom. The Law Lexicon says</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> experience means knowledge or practical wisdom gained from what one has observed, encountered or undergone.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">        </span>. . . (18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Words and Phrases </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Employment advertisement </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">When an employment advertisement stipulates</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> a particular qualification as the minimum qualification for the post and further stipulates that the qualification should be relaxed in case of special qualification/ higher qualification the only meaning of it conveys is that some additional weightage has to be given to the higher qualified candidates.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (21)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Service matter—In the absence of rule or </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">regulation selection committee do not require</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> to record seasons—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The selection has been made by the assessment of relative merits of rival candidates determined in the course of the interview of the candidates. There is no rule or regulation brought to our notice requiring the selection committee to record reasons. In the absence of any such legal requirement the selection made without recording reasons cannot be found fault with. Administrative authority is under no legal obligation to record reasons in support of its decision. Indeed, even the principles of natural justice do not require a selection committee to record reasons for the selection or non-selection of a person in the absence of statutory requirement. But ‘fairness’ or ‘fair procedure’ ought to be observed.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (22)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Shinda Hasan Vs. State of Uttar Pradesh and other AIR 1990 SC 1381 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Petitioner:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on- Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in .85pt 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondent :</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate with Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, Senior Advocate and Mr. Mehadi Hasan Chowdhury, Ms. Anita Gazi Rahman, Advocate </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in .85pt 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This petition for leave to appeal is directed against the judgment and order dated 30.08.2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.1132 of 2011 making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The facts, in brief, are that while the writ petitioner had been serving as Associate Professor in the Sylhet M.A.G. Osmani Medical College an employment notification was published for appointment in the post of Professor by the Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University (the BSMMU). In the said notification, the wanting experience, amongst others, was that the applicant must have five years experience in performing the functions as Associate Professor of that particular subject regularly or teaching experience in equal status. The writ petitioner, finding him qualified for the post, filed application stating his educational qualifications, length of experience and other particulars. Following the regular recruitment procedure, he was selected as a Professor of Surgery on 10.09.2003 by the BSMMU authority. Since the writ petitioner was in government service he filed application addressing the Secretary, Ministry of Health and Family Welfare on 22.09.2003 tendering his resignation with effect from 30.09.2003. Pursuant to his application, his resignation was accepted with effect from 30.09.2003. Getting appointment, he joined in the BSMMU on 01.10.2003. The writ petitioner had resigned from his government job without taking any financial benefit. The appointment of the writ petitioner was made in strict and full compliance of the provisions followed for appointment of a Professor of the BSMMU which was approved by the Syndicate of the BSMMU in its 16th meeting held on 03.03.2004. The service of the writ petitioner was confirmed by the Syndicate of the BSMMU on 13.08.2004 in its 21st meeting. The writ petitioner, at the time of filing application for recruitment, did not suppress anything with regard to his qualifications, experiences and publications etc. At the time of appointment of the writ petitioner, he had the highest number of post graduation degrees and he was the only person who had fellowship in colorectal surgery from the National University Hospital, Singapore. The writ petitioner earned reputation as one of the best doctors of the country. Due to his unblemished service record and ability, he was given the charge of Course Co-ordinator of all Post Graduate Courses and the Residency Programmes run by the Surgery Department of the BSMMU. During his entire service career, no question was raised with regard to his ability and competency as a doctor and a teacher. In the absence of the Chairman of the Surgery Department, he was given the charge of Chairmanship on many occasions. He was also a member of the Departmental Examination Committee. While the writ petitioner was discharging his duties with highest level of satisfaction of the BSMMU authority, all on a sudden, he was served with a notice vide an office order dated 30.06.2010 <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">under Memo No. BSMMU/2010/7060 to explain</span> as to why his appointment in the BSMMU would not be cancelled. The writ petitioner was asked to submit his reply, if any, within 7 days from the date of receipt of the order. Without considering the reply, the BSMMU authority vide the impugned order dated 22.12.2010 under Memo No. BSMMU/ 2010/12315 had terminated the writ petitioner from service in the name of ‘cancellation of appointment’ allegedly on the basis of the decision of the Syndicate dated 22.12.2010. Challenging the order of cancellation of appointment dated 22.12.2010 the writ petitioner, filing writ petition, obtained Rule Nisi.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The writ respondent Nos.1-3 contested the Rule contending that on 25.06.2003, the BSMMU authority published an advertisement for appointment of suitable candidates for the several vacant posts under the BSMMU. On 10.09.2003, the writ petitioner was selected for the post of Professor of Surgery Department by the then administration of the BSMMU. Subsequently, it was revealed that the writ petitioner had no necessary experience and qualifications for such appointment and his appointment to the post of Professor was secured not through meeting the relevant recruitment criteria but through some other means which does not necessarily make his appointment legal and hence his appointment was a nullity. During the past Care-taker Government, allegation of corruption, irregularities in purchase and recruitments were brought against the then administration of the BSMMU which were referred to the then Vice Chancellor of the University by the office of the Head of the care-taker government through the concerned Ministry. The BSMMU authority constituted a 7(seven) members Enquiry Committee vide Memo dated 06.05.2007. The Enquiry Committee, holding inquiry, submitted report on 26.07.2007 stating that the writ petitioner failed to meet the required experience to be appointed as professor and hence proper steps as per law should be taken against the appointment process of the writ petitioner. Thereafter, another 6(six) members <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Committee was formed by the then administration</span> of the BSMMU dated 05.08.2007. The Committee found that the writ petitioner did <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">not meet the experience required to be appointed</span> in the post of professor. Subsequently, the Parliamentary Standing Committee of the Ministry of Health and Family Welfare decided to hold enquire into the allegations of corruption and irregularities committed in the BSMMU and submit detailed report before the Parliamentary Standing Committee. A Sub Committee, holding inquiry, submitted a detailed report before the Standing Committee on 12.01.2010 stating, inter alia, that in the appointment process the relevant rules and regulations had not been followed. The writ petitioner was appointed despite his lacking of required experience for appointment. In that <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">report, it was recommended that the appointment</span> of writ petitioner should be cancelled since he did not hold necessary experience at the time of appointment as Professor of Surgery. On 16.05.2010 in the 38th Syndicate Meeting of the BSMMU, the authority decided to take necessary steps and to that end, writ petitioner was served with a show cause notice through the Office Order bearing Memo No. BSMMU /2010/7060 dated 30.06.2010 asking him to furnish reasons within 7(seven) days as to why his appointment in the post of Professor of Surgery should not be cancelled in view of the report of the Committee. The writ petitioner upon receiving the said show cause notice submitted his reply on 04.07.2010 and on perusal of the same the Syndicate, in its 41st meeting held on 22.12.2010, decided to cancel the appointment of the writ petitioner in the post of Professor by the impugned letter dated 22.12.2010. On 16.01.2011, upon receipt of the said cancellation letter from the university, the writ petitioner filed a Review petition to the office of Chancellor of the BSMMU through writ respondent No.3 instead of the Vice Chancellor as required under section 55 of the Act, 1998. Thereafter, the writ petitioner filed the instant writ petition and obtained Rule which was liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The High Court Division by the impugned judgment and order made the said Rule absolute. Against which, the BSMMU has filed this petition for leave to appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, learned Counsel appearing for the writ respondent-petitioner, submits that at the time of appointing the writ petitioner he had no requisite experience to be appointed in the post of Professor of the University and the then BSMMU authority most illegally appointed him as Professor of the surgery department, thus, the BSMMU authority rightly cancelled his appointment, the High Court Division erred in law in making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Probir Neogi, appearing with Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, Mr. Mehadi Hasan Chowdhury, Ms. Anita Gazi, learned Counsel for the respondent, submits that the writ petitioner-respondent had requisite qualifications and experiences to be appointed as professor of the department of the BSMMU and the BSMMU authority, being satisfied with the same and complying with all legal formalities, appointed the writ petitioner in the said post. Moreso, in the advertisement, it was mentioned that the terms and conditions as mentioned in employment notification would be relaxed for the candidate having special qualifications, the High Court Division rightly made the Rule absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">From the papers available in the record, it appears that the BSMMU authority issued employment notification under memo No</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">we Gm <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Gg Gg BD/2003/35/32</span></strong></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> dated 24.06.2003 inviting</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> application for appointment in the post of Professors and in some other posts. text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 8.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">(L) wek¡we`¨vj‡qi wb‡qvM wewa Abyhvqx wbw`©ó c‡` wb‡qv‡Mi kZ©vejx c~iY bv nIqv m‡Ë¡I GB cªv_©x‡K wbe©vPb K‡i‡Qb| G‡Z wb‡qvM KwgwUi ZrKvjxb mfvcwZ, m`m¨MY I m`m¨-mwPe wbqg msNb I KZ©e¨ Ae‡njv K‡i‡Qb e‡j cªZxqgvb nq weavq Zuv‡`i weiy‡× AvBbvbyM e¨e¯nv Mªn‡Yi mycvwik Kiv nj|</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 12.0pt 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Precisely, the allegation against the writ petitioner, as it appears from subsequent inquiry reports that at the time of getting appointment as professor in the BSMMU he had no requisite experience. More specifically, in the employment notification required experience for filing application in the post of professor was that</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">, “<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">wbw`©ó wel‡q wbqwgZ cuvP erm‡ii mn‡hvMx Aa¨vcK A_ev mgvb c` gh©v`vi wk¶KZv</strong>”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> but the writ petitioner had no such experience. He had following teaching experience at the relevant time:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 45.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(1)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor (Current charge)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 45.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Moymonshingh Medical College </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 45.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(from 01.03.1998 to 31.05.1998)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 45.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(2)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor (current charge)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 45.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">BSMMU</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 45.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(from 01.06.1998 to 09.05.2001)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt 45.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(3)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt 45.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sylhet M.A.G. Osmani Medical College</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 45.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(from 09.05.2001 to 30.09.2003)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">That is, he had 5 years 04 months 15 days teaching experience as Associate Professor in charge and Associate Professor before filing application. It appears that the writ petitioner, holding the post of Associate Professor, performed his duties more than 2 years and holding the post of Associate Professor-in-charge performed his duties for more than 3 years. Question is, whether at the time of performing his duties as Associate Professor in charge he had acquired any experience or not. According to Black’s Law Dictionary experience means a state, extent, or duration of being engaged in a particular study or work. A word implying skill, facility, or practical wisdom gained by personal knowledge, feeling, and action, and also the course or process by which one attains knowledge or wisdom. The Law Lexicon says experience means knowledge or practical wisdom gained from what one has observed, encountered or undergone. While performing the functions of a Associate professor-in-charge the same was not the substantive post of the writ petitioner but it is difficult to say conclusively that within those period he did not gather any experience as Associate Professor-in-Charge or his skill has not been improved. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have already found from the advertisement that it was mentioned specially therein that every condition is relaxable in the case of special qualifications of the candidate. <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">The exact words were,</span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> <u>“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">we‡kl †hvM¨Zvm¤úbœ cªv_©x‡`i</strong></u></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;"> †¶‡Î †h †Kvb kZ© wkw_j‡hvM¨</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">”</span></u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">.(</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">underlined by us) </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">From the required education qualifications</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> for the post of Professor in respect of clinical subject as mentioned in the employment notification issued by the BSMMU authority as well as in </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">wb‡qvM bxwZgvjv (wk¶K)</strong>t”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> were No.(1)MBBS or equal degree, (2) MD in particular subject or MS (from the BSMMU or Dhaka University)/ FCPS (Fellowship of the College of Physicians and Surgeons of Bangladesh) /MRCP, FRCS, MRCOG DMRT /DRMD/ DPM/ M/M. Phil or post graduate or any post graduate qualification in equal status. That is, the writ petitioner was entitled to file application for getting appointment in BSMMU since, at the relevant time, he had MBBS and FCPS degrees. It further appears that apart from MBBS and FCPS degrees, the writ petitioner had FRCS degree from the Royal College of Physicians and Surgeons of Glasgow, UK, MS(Surgery) from the Institute of Postgraduate Medicine and Research, Dhaka (Dhaka University), Bangladesh and Fellowship of Colorectal Surgery from the National University Hospital, Singapore. That is, he acquired specific surgical qualification, that was, Fellowship of the Royal College of Surgeons which is training in surgical specialities and which also shows his education and training, professional qualifications, and surgical competence which was given upon rigorous evaluation and which is consistent with high standards of special qualification. It further appears that in addition to his FCPS and FRCS decrees, he had also M.S. (Surgery) degree which is also a postgraduate degree and advanced qualification in surgery. The said degree is also designed to be awarded as a higher degree. That is, the writ petitioner had special qualifications to be appointed as Professor of the BSMMU. It is quite clear that the petitioner had post graduation degrees and Fellowships for meeting the eligibility criteria, for filing applications in the post of Professor. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have already found that in the advertisement it was specifically mentioned that in case of special qualifications every terms and conditions mentioned in the employment notification was relaxable. When an employment advertisement stipulates a particular qualification as the minimum qualification for the post and further stipulates that the qualification should be relaxed in case of special qualification/higher qualification the only meaning of it conveys is that some additional weightage has to be given to the higher qualified candidates. The writ petitioner had three more special qualifications, that is, FRCS, MS (Surgery) and Fellowship of colorectal surgery, National University Hospital, Singapore besides the requisite qualification as mentioned in the employment notification. From the first inquiry report held by the BSMMU it appears that the BSMMU syndicate in its 21st meeting decided that in case of specially qualified candidates the terms as provided is relaxable and in the said report it was further observed that, </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">eZ©gvb ch©v‡jvPbv KwgwU wek¡we`¨vj‡qi Rb¥j‡Mœ 30/04/1998Bs Zvwi‡L RvixK…Z ZrKvjxb wfwm AavcK Gg, G Kv‡`ix g‡nv`‡qi ¯^v¶‡i GKwU Awdm Av‡`‡k †`Lv‡Z cvq †h, mv‡eK AvBwcwRGgGÛAvi Gi 43 Rb wk¶K‡K Zuv‡`i K…Z c~e© PvKzixi PjwZ `vwqZ¡ Ges fvicªvß c‡`i AwfÁZv‡K we‡ePbv K‡i ¯e-¯e c‡` GB wek¡we`¨vj‡qi PvKzix‡Z wbqwgZ Kiv n‡q‡Q|</strong>”</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In such view of the matter, it is difficult to hold that writ petitioner’s appointment was totally illegal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have found that in another Inquiry report it has been observed, </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">ÒcwÎKvq cªKvwkZ wb‡qvM weÁwß‡Z D‡jøwLZ Ôwe‡kl †hvM¨Zv m¤úbœ cªv_©x‡`i †¶‡Î †h †Kvb kZ© wkw_j †hvM¨Õ Gi mg_©‡b cªv_©xi wK we‡kl †hvM¨Zv wQj Ges †Kvb we‡kl †hvM¨Zvi wfwË‡Z wb‡qvM kZ© wkw_j Kiv n‡qwQj wKbv, †m m¤ú‡K© wb‡qvM KwgwUi Kvh©weeibx‡Z †Kvb wKQy D‡jøL bvB|</strong>Ó”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> The selection has been made by the assessment of relative merits of rival candidates determined in the course of the interview of the candidates. There is no rule or regulation brought to our notice requiring the selection committee to record reasons. In the absence of any such legal requirment the selection made without recording reasons can not be found fault with. Administrative authority is under no legal obligation to record reasons in support of its decision. Indeed, even the principles of natural justice do not require a selection committee to record reasons for the selection or non-selection of a person in the absence of statutory requirement. But ‘fairness’ or ‘fair procedure’ ought to be observed. It is not shown that the selection was arbitrary or whimsical or the selection committee did not act fairly in appointing Dr. Zahidul Huq. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is relevant here to refer the case of Ms. Shinda Hasan V. State of Uttar Pradesh and other reported in AIR 1990 SC 1381. In the said case in response to the advertisement the appellant along with others applied for the post. The appellant did not fulfill the qualification of five years experience. She alone appeared for the interview and the Selection Committee relaxed the qualification of experience in her favour and selected her. The Management thereafter sought the approval of the University to appoint the appellant as required under section 31(11) of the Uttar Pradesh State Universities Act, 1973. The University, however, declined to approve and directed the management to re-advertise the post. The appellant challenged the decision of the University by way of a writ petition under Article 226 of the Constitution of India before the Luckhnow Bench of the Allahabad High Court on the ground that the college being a minority institution any interference by the University under the Act is violative of Article 30(1) of the Constitution. It was also contended that there was no basis of justification to withhold the approval. The High Court rejected the attack on the ground of Article 30 of the Constitution of India by holding that the provisions of the Act are regulatory and are primarily for the purpose of maintaining uniformity, efficiency and standards of education in the minority institutions. On the merits, the High Court held that the Selection Committee was not justified in relaxing the qualification without reserving that right to itself in the advertisement. The High Court also found that the qualification ‘possessing working knowledge of Urdu’ was unjust. On the above findings the writ petition was dismissed. This is how the appellant went to the Supreme Court. Supreme Court adjourned the case with the following order: ‘It is admitted by the parties that as a result of the Court orders the appellant Ms. Shainda Hasan is continuing to work as Principal in the Karamat Husain Muslim Girls College, Lucknow since 1974. Having served the institution for over 16 years it would be unjust to make her leave the post. Under the circumstances let the University reconsider the whole matter sympathetically.’” Then Indian Supreme Court of India held, </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/Downloads/Issue__September__2019(2)/Issue__September_19__C.%20P.%203832%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___1_.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Civil petition for leave to appeal No. 3832 of 2017.</span></u></em></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 30.08.2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 1132 of 2011.)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
795	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Engineer Monjurul Ahsan Munshi Vs.  The State and another</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Appeal No. 5948 of 2007  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Ruhul Quddus, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Ajmalul Hossain, Senior Advocate with Mr. Muhammad Saifullah Mamun,  Mr. Mamun Chowdhury and  Mr. Robin Rakshit, Advocates,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Engineer Monjurul Ahsan Munshi</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State and another</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Money Laundering Act, 2002 </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CRIMINAL APPEAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Ruhul Quddus, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Bishmadev Chakrabortty, J. </strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">14-16.05.2017</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/2012/September%202012/Issue%20__September__19(2)__Crl.%20Appeal.%205948%20of%2007_Md.%20Ruhul%20Quddus,%20J.__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Engineer Monjurul Ahsan Munshi</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">...Convict-Appellant </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The State and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .Respondents </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Money Launderin</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">g Act, 2002 (15 of 2003)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 2 (Ttha) (Aa)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%;">A company is always a different entity and a juristic person. The appellant being an individual and Managing Director of SBEL cannot merge into a single entity. We are, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">therefore, unable to accept that the appellant</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%;"> as an individual purchased the properties and is liable for owning/ possessing the same in </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the names of wife and son, or for concealment</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%;"> of its value. This is correct that he failed to produce any decision of the company to lend money to accused 2 for purchasing the flat at Gulshan. If any money is illegally shifted from a company’s fund, it may at best constitute an offence of money laundering as defined in section 29(Ttha) (Aa) of the Money Laundering Act, 2002 but cannot constitute an offence under section 27 of the Act V of 2004. It would also contribute in an illegality/irregularity under the Company Act and the other directors/share holders aggrieved thereby can raise the question in proper forum. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (90)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Anti-Corruption Commission Act (V of 2004)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 27</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">An offence under section 27 of the Act V of 2004 continues so long the person sought to be prosecuted owns possesses the disproportionate property as defined therein. An abetment thereto also continues in the same way with his ownership/possession over the same. There is no scope to say after acquiring the disproportionate property, time of occurrences comes to an end. Evasion of income tax and offence of acquiring/ </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">possessing/owning disproportionate property</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> by illegal means as defined in section 27 of the Act V of 2004 are not the same. There might be some professionals/businessmen who legally earn a lot of money, but pay less income tax, it is an offence of evasion of tax or suppression of facts under the income Tax Ordinance, 1984. But if any public servant or an individual acquires property by illegal means, which is apparently disproportionate to his individual acquires property by illegal means, which is apparently disproportionate to his known/ legal sources of income and fails to satisfactorily account such property, an offence under section 27 of the Act V of 2004 would be committed. In the present case, the ACC failed to prove that the appellant as an individual acquired those properties for his own benefit, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">in benami</em> of his son and wife and by illegal means, in such a case, we find no reason to convict him alone for especially when the co-accused thereselves claim it to be of their own. We are, therefore, not inclined to maintain his conviction and sentence. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . . (91 to 93)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">S.N Kabir Vs. Fateman Begum and others, 66 DLR (AD) 193; Jay Dayal Poddar (deceased) through I.Rs and another Vs. Mst. Bibi Hazra and others, AIR 1974 SC 171; Mudud Ahmed Vs. The State and another, 68 DLR (AD) 118; State Vs. Faisal Morshed Khan and another, 66 DLR (AD) 236 and Anti-Corruption Commission Vs. Dr. Mohiuddin Khan Alamgir, 62 DLR (AD) 290 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Ajmalul Hossain, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Muhammad Saifullah Mamun, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Mamun Chowdhury and </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Robin Rakshit, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Appellant</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Nazibur Rahman, Deputy Attorney General</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in .25in .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the State</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Md. Khurshid Alam Khan, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For respondent No. 2</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Ruhul Quddus, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This criminal appeal under section 10(A) of the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958(Act XL of 1958) is directed against judgment and order dated 09.10.2007 passed by the Special Judge, Court No. 5, Dhaka in Special Case No. 04 of 2007 arising out of Gulshan Police Station Case No. 101(3) 07 corresponding to GR No. 24 of 2007 convicting the appellant and sentencing him to suffer simple imprisonment for 3 (three) years under section 26(2) of the Durnity Daman Commission Ain, 2004 (Act V of 2004) read with rule 15Gha (5) of the Emergency Power Rules, 2007 (Rules, 2007) and further sentencing him to suffer rigorous imprisonment for 10 (ten) years under section 27(1) of the Act V of 2004 read with section 5(2) of the Prevention of Corruption Act, 1947 (Act II of 1947) with a fine of Taka 65,00,000/- (sixty-five lac) in default to suffer rigorous imprisonment for another one year and also <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">confiscating the properties as scheduled thereto.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Anti-Corruption Commission (ACC) received an information that the appellant himself and in the name of the members of his family was in possession of property disproportionate to his known sources of income. It thus served a notice dated 18.02.2007 under section 26(1) of the Act V of 2004 asking him to furnish statement of wealth and that of his family-members within 72 hours from receipt thereof. At that time the appellant was in Bogra jail under and order of detention. He, however, furnished the statement of wealth through his representative on 25.02.2007. On receipt of the said statement and completion of the preliminary inquiry, the ACC lodged a first information report (FIR) with Gulshan Police Station, Dhaka on 23.01.2007 under sections 26 and 27(2) of the Act V of 2004 read with section 5(2) of the Act II of 1947, section 109 of the Penal Code and rule 15Gha (5) of the Rules, 2007 against the appellant, his wife Majeda Ahsan and two sons. namely, Rezwanul Ahsan and Rezviul Ahsan bringing allegation of concealment of properties worth Taka 3,03,56,157/- (three crore three lac fifty-six thousand one hundred fifty-seven) in total and of holding properties worth Taka 4,92,13,417.73 (four crore ninety-two lac thirteen thousand four hundred seventeen and seventy-three paisa), which were dispropor-tionate to their known sources of income. The material particulars of the allegations against each of the accused were specifically described in the FIR.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The Investigating Officer (IO) investigated the case and submitted a charge sheet on 17.06.2007 against all the four FIR named accused under sections 26 and 27 of the Act V of 2004, 5(2) of the Act II of 1947, 109 of the Penal Code and rule 15Gha (5) of the Rules, 2007. According to the charge sheet, the concealed property was of Taka 3,13,93,199/- (three crore thirteen lac ninety-three thousand one hundred ninety-nine) and the disproporti-onate property, which was allegedly acquired by illegal means and beyond their legal sources of income was amounting to Taka 5,37,07,439.73 (five crore thirty-seven lac seven thousand four hundred thirty-nine and seventy-three paisa). The charge sheet was accompanied by a sanction of ACC. During investigation the accused including the appellant submitted revised statements to the ACC on 14.05.2007 in pursuance of order dated 06.05.2007 passed in Writ Petition No. 4441 of 2007.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The case being ready for trial was sent to the Senior Metropolitan Special Judge, Dhaka and was registered as Special Case No. 30 of 2007. The learned Judge took cognizance of offence against the accused including the appellant by order dated 19.06.2007 and transferred the case to the Special Judge, Court No. 5, Dhaka for trial. On transfer the case was renumbered as Special Case No. 04 of 2007. The learned Special Judge, Court No. 5 by order dated 09.07.2007 framed charge against the accused under sections 26 (2), 27(1) of the Act V of 2004 read with rule 15Gha (5) of the Rules, 2007; sections 5(2) of the Act II of 1947 and 109 of the Penal Code and proceeded with trial. The charge so framed was read over to them, to which they pleaded not guilty and claimed justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In order to prove its case the prosecution examined as many as 49 witnesses and adduced in evidence a number of documents and materials and the defence examined two witnesses including the accused 1 himself.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%;">PW1 Abu Sayed, the informant and a Deputy Director of ACC stated that on the basis of an information, it issued notice dated 18.02.2007 asking accused 1 (appellant herein) to furnish wealth statement and that of his family members. As the accused was in prison, he furnished the statement through his representative on 25.02.2007. The informant was assigned inquiry into the matter. On inquiry, he (informant) found that the accused did not furnish any statement regarding his immovable property and disclosed movable property worth Taka 80,06,353.25 (eighty lac six thousand three hundred fifty-three and twenty-five paisa), which on exclusion of debt, stood at Taka 61,28,500/- (sixty-one lac twenty-eight thousand five hundred). In the statement, he mentioned a Nisan petrol jeep (Dhaka Metro-Gha-02-1093) worth Taka 6,075,000/- but according to the record of Bangladesh Road Transport Authority (BRTA), it was valued at taka 14,25,000/-. The accused thus concealed Taka 7,50,000/- showing lesser price against the jeep. He had another Microbus (Dhaka Metro-Ttha- 11-1714), against which he mentioned Taka 1,60,000/-, but its actual price was Taka 2,35,000/-. During inquiry he was also found in possession of immovable and movable properties, which were not disclosed in the statement of wealth. He concealed property worth Taka 50.37,355/- and his total property was of Taka 1,31,40,706.06. He was paying income tax since 1983-84 having TIN No. 035-100-<span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">3258/- Company Circle-4 and he mentioned</span> his total income Taka 49,78,052.80 during the assessment years 1983-84 to 2006-07. On deduction of expenditure of Taka 14,22,432.15 his savings remained Taka 34,70,129.65 for the above period. His sources of income were remuneration from company and that of Member of Parliament. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">P.W 1 further stated that accused 2 Majeda Ahsan declared her movable and <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">immovable properties worth Taka 1,11,86,380.87.</span> On exclusion of expenditure, her savings remained Taka 80,36,380.77. She acquired four <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kathas</em> of land at Bannani in Dhaka at a consideration of Taka 5,94,808/-, which she defrayed out of income from business and constructed a three-storied building thereon in the year 1985-86 spending Taka 10,07,967/-. The Chief Engineer of Public Works Department (PWD) was requested to assess the actual cost of the building and accordingly, an Executive Engineer, PWD assessed the cost at Taka 50,97,248/-. The amount of concealment on this item was Taka 40,89,281/-. She also got a two-storied building at village Gunaighar under Debidwar police Station that was built in 2005 and declared Taka 31,50,000/- to have been spent for construction of the building. The said building was surrounded by boundary walls and there were adjacent garden, swimming pool etcetera, against which the value shown appeared to be meager. The Executive Engineer, PWD, Comilla Division assessed its cost at Taka 1,24,81,051/-. Concealment of actual cost was apparent on this item too. She had another undeclared property, namely, Flat No.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>6-J, Plot No. 20 commonly known as Green Palace at Road No. 129, Gulshan, Dhaka which she purchased from Amin Mohammad Foundation giving initial booking in the name of her sister Masuma Haque paying Taka 22,00,000/- through a cheque from Account No. 2737 of Rupali Bank, Ibrahim Mansion Branch maintained by accused 1. She, however, ultimately took the flat in her name. She also did not declare the electrical appliances used in her residence at Banani and consequently the Executive Engineer, PWD, EM Division-3 assessed the value of those appliances at Taka 25,26,450/- . Besides, there were furniture worth Taka 13,32,600/-, of which some were foreign origin brought by her son and on exclusion of the value of those foreign furniture worth Taka 8,13,200/-, concealment against the furniture stood at Taka 5,19,400/-. The value of her undeclared property thus came to Taka 62,52,100/- in terms of money and the total property found in her possession was of Taka 3,88,66,602.77, whereas she declared her income during the assessment years 1986-87 to 2006-07 to the tune of Taka 27,89,200/- only. On deduction of expenditure, her savings as per income tax file remained Taka 20,45,850/- for that period. It was thus presumed that she acquired property worth taka 3,68,20,752.77 illegally. She was a housewife having no income other than the house rents. In fact accused 1 acquired the properties by illegal means and for the purpose of concealment, had shown it in the name of his wife accused 2 Majeda Ahsan. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">PW 1 then stated that the property as declared by accused 3 Rezwanul Ahsan, excluding debt, was to Taka 36,98,700/- Besides, he was owning shares of Taka 1,20,000/- in Titas Engineering Enterprise Ltd and deposited Taka 20,71,290/- as premium against Insurance Policy No. 5003995 in ALICO. His undeclared property was of Taka 21,91,290/-, which being added with the declared property, his total property came to Taka 58,89,990/-. He was paying income tax from 1989-90 having TIN No. 035-100-4732/- Company-4 and mentioned his total income to the tune of Taka 19,92,000/- during<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the assessment years 1989-90 to 2006-07, On exclusion of expenditure, his savings remained Taka 13,59,800/-. He thus acquired property worth Taka 11,40,190/- illegally. He had no other income except remuneration from the company. In fact the property was acquired by accused 1, who with an intention to conceal his illegal <span style="letter-spacing: -.1pt;">income had shown it to have been earned by his eldest son Rezwanul Ahsan, accused 3.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 1. also stated that accused 4 Rezviul Ahsan disclosed his movable and immovable properties worth Taka 17,38,178/-. On exclusion of debt, his total property came to Taka 5,69,378.01 in terms of money. But he was found in possession of shares worth Taka 1,20,000/- in Titas Engineering Enterprise Ltd and that of Taka 1,81,7000/- in National Credit and Commerce Bank Ltd (NCCBL). He deposited premium of Taka 22,98,090/- against Life Insurance Policy No. 514176 in ALICO. His undeclared property was of Taka 25,99,790/-, which being added with the declared property, came to Taka 31,67,168.01 in total. He became an assess in the assessment year 1989-90 having TIN No. 035-1003246/Company Circle-4 and he mentioned his total income to the tune of Taka 19,92,000/- up to 2006-07. On deduction of expenditure, his savings remained Taka 15,87,270/-. He thus acquired property worth Taka 15,81,898.01 illegally. He had no other income than the wages from company. In fact accused 1 in order to conceal his illegal income had <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">shown those properties to have been earned by his youngest son Rezviul Ahsan, accused 4.</span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">PW 1 found Taka 3,35,60,157/- as total value of concealed property in names of the accused and further found their total property worth Taka 4,92,13,717.73, which was disproportionate to their known sources of income. He lodged the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ejahar</em> after obtaining permission from the Commission vide memo no. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">`y`K/58-2007(Aby-2)15087</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> dated 25.03.2007.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In cross-examination PW 1 stated of visiting the house of the accused at village Gunaighar at Debidwar, where he found a pond having its bank and quae covered with glazed tiles. As regard accused 3 he (PW 1) stated that this accused had been in America for study and he brought a car there from by his earning abroad. He also expressed his ignorance about the declaration of shares in Titas Engineering Enterprise Ltd and premium of Taka 20,00,000/- deposited in ALICO. Her expenditure up to that period was shown Taka 6,39,000/-. Accused 3 disclosed his income as Taka 19,92,000/- up to 2006-07 and Taka 6,07,000/- as expenditure. Accused 4 disclosed Taka 19,92,000/- as his income up to 2006-07 and Taka 4,02,000/- as expenditure. Both of them mentioned the remunerations from company as their sources of income. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 37 N M Al-Marin, Income tax Inspector of Company Circle-4 stated that the tax files of all the four accused were seized under a seizure list on 14.05.2007 by Akter Hossain, Deputy Director of ACC. He proved the seizure list (exhibit-19) and his signature thereon. PW 38 Saiful Islam Khan, an Office Assistant-cum-Typist of the same office deposed in support of the seizure as stated by PW 37. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 39 M A Wahab, Deputy General Manager of Rupali Bank Ltd. Ibrahim Mansion Corporate Branch stated that he was posted to the said branch at the material time. Akter Hossain, Deputy Director of ACC came to his office on 17.05.2007 and seized some documents under a seizure list against Current Account No. 2737 maintained by Superior Builders and Engineers Ltd (SBEL). He proved the seizure list and his signature thereon. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In cross examination he stated that the account was operated by accused 1, who did it in the capacity of Managing Director of SBEl. The company paid Taka 22,00,000/- to Amin Mohammad Real Estate through a cheque on 04.06.1995. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 40 Jahangir and PW 41 Khaled Hossain, two Senior Officers of the same branch of Rupali Bank Ltd. deposed in support of the seizure as stated by PW 39. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 42 A. Wadud, Director (Admin) of the ACC stated that accused 1 submitted his wealth statement through Advocate Rezaul Karim. Subsequently he furnished a revised statement on 14.05.2007 through his agent Rezviul Ahsan in pursuance of an order passed in Writ Petition No. 4441 of 2007. He proved the statements (exhibits-21 and 23). </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">PW 43 M.
