Court Division for the purpose of conferring the said jurisdiction on its subordinate Court, (b) if a party to the arbitration agreement, initially, approaches the District Judge Court for appointment of an arbitrator and, later on, his challenge about the competency and impartiality of an arbitrator before the arbitral tribunal fails, will he approach the District Judge Court ignoring the specific appellate jurisdiction of the High Court Division conferred upon it by Section 14(4) of the Arbitration Act, (c) when a foreign party of a civil suit pending in the District Judge Court makes an application for staying the proceedings under Section 10 of the Arbitration Act, will the foreign party file application for interim Order in the District Judge Court, in the backdrop of existence of the provisions of Section 7A of the Arbitration Act, which requires that the High Court Division shall hear such application, (d) when a party to the arbitration, at first, approaches the District Judge Court either for obtaining interim Order under Section 7A of the Arbitration Act or makes application under Section 10 of the Arbitration Act in the District Judge Court for staying proceedings of the civil suit pending therein or asks the District Judge Court to appoint the arbitrator under Section 12 of the Arbitration Act and, then, during pendency of the arbitral proceeding, if he wants to challenge the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal in a Court, not in the arbitral tribunal under Section 17 of the Arbitration Act, will the provisions of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act be of any use for him to approach the Court of District Judge, in other words, will the jurisdiction and power of the High Court Division under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act be ipso facto conferred upon and exercised by the District Judge Court and (e) when a party<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to the arbitral proceedings approaches the District Judge Court invoking Section 21(4) of the Arbitration Act for enforcement of the interim Order, whether any party to the said arbitration is barred from approaching the High Court Division by the provisions of Section 53 of the Arbitration Act for making applications under Section 7A, 10, 12 &amp; 20 of the Arbitration Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">There are two vital aspects of the provisions of Section 53 of the Arbitration Act. The first aspect is that through its non-obstante provisions, it seeks to herald that irrespective of any statements, stipulations and provisions to the contrary made in the Arbitration Act, or any other law, the provisions of Section 53 of the Arbitration Act shall stand. The second aspect is - if any party to the arbitration agreement registers its name in a Court for any purpose, that Court shall assume jurisdiction over the arbitration agreement and arbitral agreement in whose connection a party have moved before the Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Now, the question comes up for consideration as to whether the jurisdiction conferred specifically upon, and the power vested exclusively in, the High Court Division vide Sections 7A, 10, 12, 14(4) &amp; 20 of the Arbitration Act can be discarded by a non-obstante provision, and that too for the purpose of endowing a sub-ordinate Court with the said jurisdiction and power of the High Court Division. While as a normal course of action, the Legislature does not go for enactment of a law by which the superior Court’s jurisdiction and power will be scrapped or curtailed in order to enrich and empower the sub-ordinate Courts with the said jurisdiction and power, yet if the Legislature in their wisdom considers it necessary, they are competent to enact such law. However, this sort of enactment is normally made by the Legislature in clearer and specific expressions and, furthermore, in passing such laws the Parliament usually tables some explanations before the House.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Given the fact that in Section 53 of the Arbitration Act, the Legislature has incorporated the word “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">†Kv‡bv Av`vj‡Z</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">” (in a Court), and Section 2(b) of the Arbitration Act defines “Court” means “<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">District Judge’s Court and includes Additional District Judge’s Court appointed by the Government for discharging the functions of District Judge’s Court under this Act through Gazette notification</em>”, it is difficult for anyone to comprehend the literal meaning. Because, though in ordinary sense the High Court Division is also a Court, but the Legislature consciously has not included the High Court Division as the ‘Court’ in Section 2(b), rather the Parliament has provided a separate definition of the ‘High Court Division’ in Section 2(q) in the following terms; “<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">High Court Division means High Court Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh</em>”. Therefore, this Court is led to hold that ‘Court’ means District Judge Court and, thus, the literal meaning should be that whenever any party to an arbitration agreement will take recourse to the Court of District Judge of any particular District, the said District Judge Court shall have the exclusive jurisdiction over the said arbitration matter up to the period of final termination of the arbitral proceedings, and not any other District Judge Court. The specific jurisdictions conferred upon the High Court Division, thus, are not meant to have been taken away by the provisions of Section 53 of <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the Arbitration Act. The golden rule of statutory</span> interpretation is that when any ambiguity appears in a provision of a statute, the first option for the Court is to find out its literal meaning. And, in the event that it becomes a <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">complex task for the Court to go with the above</span> rule, only then, the Court would endeavour to discover its meaning with the help of the preamble and other provisions of the concerned statute without making any of its provisions nugatory. In this case, if this Court interprets the word “Court” to be the all types of Court, then, while on the one hand, Sections 2(b) &amp; 2(q) shall turn to be superfluous, on the other hand, the specific jurisdiction conferred upon the High Court Division will be abridged abruptly.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Having held as above, I find that since it is beyond the jurisdiction of the Court of District Judge, Dhaka to decide on the issue of the competency, impartiality of the arbitrators and to rule on the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal, the petitioner’s apparent fora for that purpose are (i) the arbitral tribunal itself and (ii) the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Given the fact that the respondent no. 4 has approached the Court of the District Judge for enforcement of the interim Order passed by the arbitral tribunal under Section 21(4) of the Arbitration Act and the said Court being incapable of assuming jurisdiction under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act, the petitioner <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">has nothing to agitate before the aforesaid Court.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The sixth issue is whether this Court is competent to entertain and adjudicate upon the question relating to jurisdiction of arbitration tribunal. Since the petitioner’s apparent fora for addressing his grievances are either the arbitral tribunal to invoke the provisions of Sections 14(2) and 17(b) of the Arbitration Act or the High Court Division to invoke Section 20 of the Arbitration Act and, seemingly, the petitioner availed himself of the forum of the High Court Division, thus, at this stage, it would be profitable if the provisions of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act are examined by the Court. Section 20 of the Arbitration Act runs as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">20. Powers of the High Court Division in deciding jurisdiction-</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">(1) The High Court Division may, on the application of any of the parties to the arbitration agreement, after serving notice upon all other parties, determine any question as to the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No application under this section shall be taken into account, unless the High Court Division is satisfied that-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo4; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The determination of the question is likely to produce substantial savings in costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo4; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">the application was submitted without any delay; and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo4; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">there is good reason why the matter should be decided by the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The application shall state-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The reasons on which the matter should be decided by the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(4)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Unless otherwise agreed by the parties, where any application is pending before the High Court Division under this section, the arbitral tribunal shall continue arbitration proceedings and make an arbitral award.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">From a minute reading of the entire provisions of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act, my understanding is that sub-Section (1) of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act is the provision which enables and empowers the High Court Division to entertain an application from any party to the arbitration agreement regarding jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal, subject to fulfilling the conditions set out in sub-Section (2) of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act. Thus, a petitioner, who has invoked Section 20 of the Arbitration Act, is under a mandatory obligation to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>satisfy the High Court Division that all the conditions stipulated in clauses (a) to (c) of Section 20(2) of the Arbitration Act are satisfied before entertaining or registering an application. In other words, the power invested in the High Court Division for entertaining an application under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act is not an independent power, for, it can be exercised by the High Court Division only upon being satisfied that (a) the determination of the question is likely to produce substantial savings in costs, (b) the application was submitted without any delay and (c) there is good reason why the matter should be decided by the Court. Therefore, the High Court Division’s power having been circumscribed by Section 20(2) of the Arbitration Act, an application under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act should be taken into account by the Court only after being satisfied as to fulfilling the conditions set out in clauses (a) to (c) of Section 20(2) of the Arbitration Act. Additionally, the petitioner is also required to state the reasons/arguments/ grounds, based on which the High Court Division would dispose of the application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">From a meticulous scrutiny of the averments made in this application and careful examination of the annexed papers, I did not find that filing of the instant application before the High Court Division helped the petitioner or the respondents to save costs, nor did I find that the application was filed without squandering time inasmuch as the interim Order was passed by the arbitral tribunal on 02.08.2018, whereas the present application has been filed on 30.08.2018, save and except finding that the petitioner has placed before this Court some reasons as to why the question of jurisdiction should be adjudicated upon by this Court. However, Section 20(2) of the Arbitration Act requires that the petitioner must simultaneously satisfy all the three conditions laid down in clauses (a) to (c) thereof, for, none of the clauses (a) to (c) ends up with the word ‘or’. Since the petitioner has failed to satisfy this Court about how he is saving costs by invoking the provisions of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act and, also, since the petitioner approached this Court after nearly one month of passing the interim Order of the arbitral tribunal, I find that the petitioner ought to have challenged the jurisdiction of the tribunal before the arbitration tribunal. Therefore, this Court is led to hold that the instant application cannot be entertained for adjudication upon the question of jurisdiction of the tribunal and the interim Order passed by this Court at the time of admission of this matter on 03.09.2018, is liable to be vacated. Furthermore, in view of the stipulations made in sub-Section (4) of Section 20 of the Arbitration Act by the Legislature that <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“unless otherwise agreed by the parties, where any application is pending before the High Court Division under this Section, the arbitral tribunal shall continue arbitration proceedings and make an arbitral award”,</em> the arbitral tribunal is under an obligation to continue with the arbitration proceedings towards disposing of the arbitration pending before it.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The<span style="color: red;"> seventh</span> issue is whether the petitioner has waived his right to challenge the appointment of the arbitrators and, also, whether he has waived his right to object to the impugned interim Order. The above issue has to be framed by this Court in order to address the submissions of the learned Advocate for the respondent no. 4 with reference to the provisions of Section 6 of the Arbitration Act and the case of Joinal Abedin Jamal Vs Noor Afzal 63 DLR 432. Let me, therefore, see the provisions of Section 6 of the Arbitration Act, which run as follows: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 30.0pt; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">6. Waiver of right to object</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-A party who knows that-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo2; tab-stops: 48.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">any provision of this Act from which the parties may derogate, or</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo2; tab-stops: 48.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 30.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">any requirement under the arbitration agreement, has not been complied with and yet proceeds with the arbitration without stating his objection to such non-compliance <u>without undue delay or, if a time limit is provided thereof within such period of time</u>, shall be deemed to have waived his right to so object.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">From a careful reading of the provisions of Section 6 of the Arbitration Act, it appears to this Court that when a party before the arbitral tribunal does not raise any objection with regard to non-compliance of any provision of the Arbitration Act or with regard to non-fulfillment of any requirement set out in the arbitration agreement within the time prescribed in the Arbitration Act and/or within the time-limit stipulated in the arbitration agreement or, in the absence of any stipulation as to the time in the law or in the arbitration agreement, within a reasonable time without making any delay, for dealing with that scenario, the Legislature mandated the arbitral tribunal and the Courts to take a presumption that the aforesaid party has waived his right to so object.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The crucial aspect of the provisions of <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Section 6 is, thus, the time to raise such objection,</span> which is required to be prescribed either in the law or to be stipulated in the arbitration agreement. Since in this case, the petitioner is raising question about appointment of arbitrators towards the formation of the arbitral tribunal in question, the respondents are taking a plea that the petitioner, by not raising the objection immediately after knowing about the appointment of the arbitrators or soon after passing the impugned interim order dated 02.08.2018, has waived his right.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Upon skimming through the provisions (a) relating to appointment of arbitrators, (b) regarding raising challenge as to holding the position of the arbitrator and (c) about raising question as to the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal, it appears to this Court that no time-frame is prescribed in the law for raising an objection as to appointment of the members of the arbitral tribunal, nor is there any such stipulation in the arbitration agreement executed by the partners of the MSC (the petitioner and the respondent no. 4) and, therefore, the only tool to assess the time limit is whether the petitioner has made undue delay in raising objection as to the appointment of arbitrators and formation of the arbitral tribunal. This Court’s view is that since the parties to the ongoing arbitration proceedings are yet to file their respective written pleadings before the arbitral tribunal, there has not been any such delay in raising the objection as to appointment of the arbitrators or as to the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal which can be termed as undue or unreasonable. In the cited case of Joinal Abedin Jamal Vs Noor Afza 63 DLR 432, the aggrieved party raised objection as to appointment of the arbitrator after passing the award by the arbitral tribunal, and that too before the Execution Court, which led this Court to hold that by not raising the objection as to the appointment of the arbitrator before the arbitral tribunal within a reasonable time, the Court deems that the party has waived his right to raise such objection as to the appointment of arbitrators or jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">I would finally take up the last three issues, being issue nos. viii, ix &amp; x, together for the sake of their better resolution. The issues are whether the present Members and the Chairman of arbitral tribunal should continue to perform their functions, whether this Court should constitute/create a new arbitral tribunal and whether the Arbitration </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Miscellaneous Case No. 501/18 pending before the Court of District Judge, Dhaka should be kept in abeyance, so that the new arbitrators may review the impugned interim Order passed by the arbitration tribunal on 02.08.2018</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">. The above issues have been framed by this Court to consider the suggestions proposed by the arbitrators before this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">In order to deal with these three issues, I need to sum up the findings made by this Court hereinabove. The findings of this Court on the 7 (seven) issues so far dealt with by this Court are: (a) there is existence of an arbitration agreement between the partners of the MSC (i.e. between the petitioner and the respondent no. 4) and they are bound to resolve their dispute through the arbitration, (b) the arbitral tribunal is a valid one and the tribunal lawfully passed the impugned interim Order, (c) for resolution of the petitioner’s grievance, the apparent fora are either the arbitral tribunal for invocation of the provisions of Section 14(2) of the Arbitration Act and Section 17 of the Arbitration Act or the High Court Division for seeking a ruling on the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act, (d) the petitioner’s instant application under Section 20 of the Arbitration Act cannot be entertained by this Court, (e) the petitioner has not waived his right to object to the appointment of arbitrator nor has he waived his right to raise objection as to the jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal and (f) the Court of District Judge is not competent to hear and adjudicate upon the issues of appointment of arbitrators or jurisdiction of the arbitral tribunal. Now, the only option remains for the petitioner to go back to the arbitral tribunal and file application before it either under Section 14(2) of the Arbitration Act or under Section 17 of the Arbitration Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">After delivering of the Judgment with regard to the core issues of this case, namely, issue nos. (i) to (vii), this Court expressed its opinion in the open-Court addressing the parties of this case that although this Court has held hereinbefore that the tribunal has been formed lawfully and the interim Order passed by the said tribunal is also valid, however, this Court is going to afford this petitioner Mr. Ghulam Mohiuddin (Bhutto) an opportunity to approach the tribunal with an application for reviewing the tribunal’s Order dated 02.08.2018. At this juncture, this Court reminded both the parties that as per the prayers of both the parties this Court has adjudicated upon the core issues. Now, it is up to the parties to resolve the dispute either through the arbitral tribunal constituted by the present arbitrators or through reconstituting the arbitral tribunal as per the suggestions put forward by the arbitrators when they appeared before this Court. This Court opined that it would be fair for all the parties if the tribunal is reconstituted with one nominated person from each of the side and the Chairman is appointed by this Court. If they wish to resolve the dispute through a reconstituted arbitral tribunal by appointing any one from the concerned arbitrators, they must first take consent from the present arbitrator/s and, in the event that s/he would be comfortable to work with the newly appointed members and Chairman, only then his/her name may be proposed by the parties as the member of the reconstituted tribunal. In reply thereto, after consulting with the present arbitrators and also receiving the instructions from their respective clients, Mr. Tanvir Parvez, the learned Advocate for the petitioner proposes the name of Mr. Debborata Laha, son of Promod Chandra Laha &amp; Maya Rani Banik, RM Center (4<sup>th</sup> Floor), 101 Gulshan Avenue, Dhaka-1212 (Contact: 01978-004545) as the arbitrator of the petitioner, Mr. Ghulam Mohiuddin (Bhutto) and Ms. Faria Huq, the learned Advocate for the respondent no. 4, proposes the name of Mr. Afzal Husain Choudhury, son of late Abdul Hossain Chowdhury, House No. 55, Road No. 4A, Dhanmondi, Dhaka-1209 (Contact: 01714-004587) as the arbitrator of the respondent no. 4, Mr. Zahed Obaidul Huq Chowdhury. Pursuant to obtaining two names from the two sides, this Court asked both the sides as to whether they wish to appoint the Chairman of the tribunal from the retired Hon’ble Chief Justices or from the former Hon’ble Judges of either Division of the Supreme Court or from the learned Advocates of this Bar. It was notified to them that an Hon’ble Chief Justice (retired) should be remunerated more or less Tk. 25,00,000/- (twenty five lacs) and an Hon’ble Judge (retired) of either Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh should not be paid less than Tk. 10,00,000/- (ten lacs). They opted to appoint a former Hon’ble Chief Justice. This Court then announced Mr. Md. Muzammel Hossain, the former Hon’ble Chief Justice of Bangladesh, as the Chairman of the arbitral tribunal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Upon arriving at the above consensus through taking necessary consents and instructions from the partners of the MSC and the present arbitrators, this Court is of the view that the present application may be disposed of with a direction upon the District Judge Court, Dhaka outlining his next course of action with regard to the Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018 and, also, upon the arbitral tribunal as to the time-limit for conclusion of the arbitration proceedings. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 30.0pt list .5in; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The Arbitration Application No. 14 of 2018 is, thus, disposed of without any order as to costs with the following observations, Orders and directions;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(i)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Since the interim Order dated 12.08.2018 passed by the learned District Judge, Dhaka in Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018 has already expired, there is no need to pass any Order for staying its operation. In other words, the interim Order dated 02.08.2018 shall not be enforced until the same is endorsed by the reconstituted arbitral tribunal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(ii)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned Advocates for both the sides are hereby directed to notify their respective parties regarding appointment of the Chairman of the reconstituted arbitral tribunal. They are further directed to contact Mr. Justice Md. Muzammel Hossain, the former Hon’ble Chief Justice of Bangladesh (01787662239) and supply him a copy of this Judgment, so that he can take necessary preparation towards having first sitting of the reconstituted tribunal with the members at his earliest convenience.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(iii) </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned District Judge, Dhaka shall not proceed with the Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018 under Section 21(4) of the Arbitration Act till receiving an Order from the reconstituted arbitral tribunal on the application proposed to be filed by Mr. Ghulam Mohiuddin (Bhutto) for reviewing the interim Order dated 02.08.2018 passed by the arbitral tribunal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(iv)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The reconstituted arbitral tribunal shall be completely free and independent to hear the application proposed to be filed by Mr. Ghulam Mohiuddin (Bhutto) and to pass an appropriate Order on that application for reviewing the interim Order dated 02.08.2018.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(v)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">If the said interim Order dated 02.08.2018 is kept intact by this reconstituted arbitral tribunal, in that event, the learned District Judge shall resume its functions to deal with the proceedings of Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018, and in the event the reconstituted arbitral tribunal modifies/alters the said Order dated 02.08.2018, in that event, the Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018 shall stand dismissed. However, in that scenario, the respondent no. 4 shall submit a certified copy of the arbitral tribunal’s Order before the Court of District Judge, Dhaka, which shall, thereupon, close the Arbitration Miscellaneous Case No. 501 of 2018 recording an appropriate Order. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo5; margin: 0in 0in 8.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(vi)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The arbitral tribunal shall endeavor to commence the proceeding formally at the end of September, 2019 and, thereafter, put in its best efforts to conclude the arbitration proceedings preferably within 6 (six) months from the date of its formal commencement. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Office is directed to send a copy of this Judgment to Mr. Justice Md. Muzammel Hossain, the former Hon’ble Chief Justice of Bangladesh and to the learned District Judge, Dhaka at once for their information and necessary action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/2012/September%202012/Issue%20__September__19(2)__Arbitration__14%20of%2018_Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Arbitration App</span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">lication No. 14 of 2018</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
797	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Secretary, Ministry of Fisheries Vs. Abdur Razzak &amp; ors</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL NO. 460 OF 2017   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Hasan Foez Siddique, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Attorney General, with Mr. Biswajit Debnath, D.A.G &amp; Mr. Samarandra Nath Biswas, D.A.G, instructed by Ms. Mahmuda Begum, Advocate-on-Record. ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ (AD)</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  The Secretary, Ministry of Fisheries and Livestock &amp; others:</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Abdur Razzak and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Evidence Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 104.9pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top" width="140"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, C,J. padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Secretary, Ministry of Fisheries and Livestock &amp; others:</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . <u>Appellant.</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C. A. No. 460/17)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Secretary, Ministry of Fisheries and Livestock &amp; others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . <u>Petitioners</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C.R.P.No.181/18)</span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Abdur Razzak and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . <u>Respondents</u></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C. A. No. 460/17)</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Ashraf-Uz-Zaman others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . <u>Respondents.</u></span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C.R.P. No. 181/18)</span></em></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 12.0pt .85pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 115</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Estoppel Explained—The basic principle is that the plea of estoppel cannot be raised to defeat the provisions of statute. The rule of promissory estoppel cannot be invoked for the enforcement of a promise which is contrary to law or outside the authority of the persons making the promise. Such principle cannot be used or invoked to compel the Government or public authority to act contrary to law or against a statute. There is no estoppel against law and at any rate the abstention of the Government in absorbing the writ petitioners in the revenue budget does not attract the law of estoppel. The Court will refuse to invoke the principles of promissory estoppel/equitable estoppel since there are specific laws providing the procedures of appointment in the posts for which the writ petitioners were seeking absorption. Such doctrine cannot be allowed to operate so as to override the clear words of statute.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                           </span>. . .(47)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Legitimate Expectation—</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">An expectation, fulfillment of which requires that a decision-maker should take an unlawful decision cannot be said to a legitimate expectation.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (58)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The doctrine of legitimate expectation can neither preclude legislation nor invalidate a statute enacted by the competent legislature. The theory of legitimate expectation cannot defeat or invalidate a legislation which is </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">otherwise valid and constitutional. Legitimate</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> expectations must be consistent with statutory provisions. The doctrine can be invoked only if it is founded on the sanction of law. Clear statutory words override any expectation, however well-founded.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is open to the Government to frame, reframe, change or recharge its policy. If the policy is changed by the Government and the Court do not find the action malafide or otherwise unreasonable, the doctrine of legitimate expectation does not make the decision vulnerable. The choice of policy is for the decision maker and not for the Court.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">When a person enters a temporary employment or gets engagement as a contractual employee and such engagement is not based on legally approved selection process as recognized by the rules or procedure, he is aware of the consequences of the appointment being temporary or contractual in nature. Such a </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">person cannot invoke the theory of legitimate</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> expectation for being regularized in the post when an appointment to the post could be made only by following the legally approved procedure for selection provided in the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Rules quoted earlier. Since the recommendation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of Public Service Commission is statutory </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">requirement, before regularization of service,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> such recommendation must be accorded.</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>. . . (56, 57 and 65)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Regularization cannot be claimed as a matter</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> of right. Recruitment should be made according to valid procedure— </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Policy </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">decision once taken should apply equaly and uniformly. Simultaneously, it is to be remembered that absorption of project employees, who obtained employment by taking recourse to back door method, is violative of the constitutional scheme as the appointments have to be made on merits of the candidates. Finally, such absorption and thereafter, regularization must be processed </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">and done following the Government instructions</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">as well as the statutory provisions as mentioned</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> earlier.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> . . . (69)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Constitution Bangladesh 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">No court can direct the Government or its instrumentalities to regularize the service of </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the officers and employees of the development</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> project in the revenue budget in the cases where statutory requirements have not been fulfilled. Regularization cannot be claimed </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">as a matter of right. It is statutory requirement</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> that opportunity shall be given to eligible persons by public notification and recruitment should be according to the valid procedure and appointment should be of the qualified persons found fit for appointment to a post or an office under the Government. When the High Court Division is approached for relief by filing writ petition, necessarily the High Court Division has to ask itself whether the person before it had any legal right to be enforced or not. It can not be directed to devise a third mode of selection.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, it is observed that:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The legitimate expectation would not override the statutory provision. The doctrine of legitimate expectation cannot be invoked for creation of posts to facilitate absorption in the offices of the regular cadres/non cadres. Creation of permanent posts is a matter for the employer and the same is based on policy decision.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">While transferring any development project and its manpower to revenue budget the provisions provided in the notifications, government orders and circulars quoted earlier must be followed. However, it is to be remembered that executive power can be exercised only to fill in the gaps and the same cannot and should not supplant the law, but only supplement the law.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Before regularization of service of the officers and employees of the development project in the revenue budget the provisions of applicable “Bidhimala” must be complied with. Without exhausting the applicable provisions of the “Bidhimala” as quoted above no one is entitled to be regularised in the service of revenue budget since those are statutory provisions.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The appointing authority, while regularising the officers and employees in the posts of revenue budget, must comply with the requirements of statutory rules in order to remove future complication. The officers and employees of the development project shall get age relaxation for participation in selection process in any post of revenue budget as per applicable Rules.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">A mandamus cannot be issued in favour of the employees directing the government and its instrumentalities to make anyone regularized in the permanent posts as of right. Any appointment in the posts described in the schedule of Bangladesh Civil Service Recruitment Rules, 1981, Gazetted Officers (Department of Live Stock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1984 and Non-gazetted Employees (Department of Live Stock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1985 bypassing Public Service Commission should be treated as back door appointment and such appointment should be stopped.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">To become a member of the service </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">in a substantive capacity, appointment</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> by the President of the Republic shall be preceded by selection by a direct recruitment by the PSC. The </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Government has to make appointment</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> according to recruitment Rules by </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">open competitive examination through</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> the PSC.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Opportunity shall be given to eligible persons by inviting applications through public notification and appointment should be made by regular recruitment through the prescribed agency following legally approved method consistent with the requirements of law.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is not the role of the Courts to encourage or approve appointments made outside the constitutional scheme and statutory provisions. It is not proper for the Courts to direct </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">absorption in permanent employment</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of those who have been recruited without following due process of selection as envisaged by the constitutional scheme.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the discussion made above and since it is not apparent from the judgment of the High Court Division and other materials available in the record that the procedure provided in the Government notification, circulars or orders and the process of appointment indicated in the “Bidhimalas” 1995 or 2005 have been followed duly for appointing the writ petitioners and that they are no longer in service in view of terms of appointment letters and contracts, the direction of the High Court Division to absorb/regularise their service giving continuity of the same can not be approved. So, the same is set aside.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> . . . (69 to 72)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">State of Karnataka Vs. Umadevi, (2006) 4 SCC page 1</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">; </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Union of India and others Vs. Hindustan Development Corporation and others, (1993) 4 SCC 433</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">; </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Punjab Communications Ltd. Vs. No. 181/18)</span><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:112%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.3pt'>) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:112%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.3pt'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">: Mr. Probir Neogi,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Senior Advocate instructed by Ms. Madhumalati Chowdhury Barua, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">JUDGMENT</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Civil Appeal No.460 of 2017 has arisen out of the judgment and order dated 07.09.2016 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.7166 of 2015. Civil Review Petition No.181 of 2018 has arisen out of the order dated 21.08.2017 passed by this Division in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal (CPLA) No.1790 of 2017. The civil appeal as well as the review petition originate from the impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.7166 of 2015 and so, both the matters have been heard together and are being disposed of by this common judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The respondents of Civil Appeal No.460 of 2017 and Civil Review Petition No.181 of 2018, as writ petitioners, filed Writ Petition No.7166 of 2015 in the High Court Division stating, inter alia, that the writ petitioners were appointed in the “Small Scale Dairy and Poultry Farmers Support Services in 22 Selected Districts Project” (herein after referred to as the Project) in 5 different categories of posts and on different dates under the Ministry of Fisheries and Livestock (shortly, the Ministry) through written and viva-voce examinations. Writ Petitioner Nos.1-13 have been working as Veterinary Surgeons, Writ Petitioner Nos.14-21 have been working as Scientific Officers, Writ Petitioner Nos.22-26 have been working as Animal Production Officers, Writ Petitioner Nos.27-40 have been working as Veterinary Compounders and Writ Petitioner Nos.41-46 have been working as Laboratory Technicians.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The first phase of the Project had started on 01.01.2010 and ended on 30.06.2013. Thereafter, it was extended for 1 year up to 30.06.2014 and then it was extended for further 1 year till 30.06.2015. Even after completion of the Project, the writ petitioners are still serving in their respective posts. According to the Project proposal (shortly, the PP), the writ-petitioners were supposed to be transferred to the revenue budget inasmuch as the PP contained that after completion of the Project, the assets and manpower would be transferred to the revenue budget. Clause 4.3(M) of the decision of the Executive Committee of National Economic Council (ECNEC) dated 31.12.2007, was amended and it was circulated by the Planning Division vide Memo No.</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
