text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">P| cªKí †gqv` †k‡l Pzw³cÎ PvKzix n‡Z Ae¨vnwZ cÎ wn‡m‡e MY¨ n‡e|</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Each of the appointees, thereafter, executed an agreement specifically stipulating that,</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒcªKí †gqv` †k‡l GB Pzw³cÎB Ae¨vnwZ cÎ wnmv‡e Mb¨ n‡e|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The conditions of service of officers and employees appointed to the temporary posts of project are to be regulated by the terms of the contract and appointment letter.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">63.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have already found that there is specific laws in the names of the Gazetted Officers (Department of Livestock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1984, the Non-Gazetted Employees (Department of Livestock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1985 and the Bangladesh Civil Service, Recruitment Rules, 1981 for the purpose of appointment of the officers in the Department of Livestock Service of the Government. All those laws categorically provide that the Public Service Commission shall recommend the best candidates on holding legally approved rigorous selection process for appointment to be made by President of the Republic. The Public Service Commission is to ensure selection of best available persons for appointment to a post to avoid arbitrariness and nepotism in the matter of appointment. The PSC is constituted by persons of high ability, varied experience and of undisputed integrity and further assisted by <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">experts on the subject. Whenever the Government</span> is required to make an appointment to a high public office, it is required to consult the PSC. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">64.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The instant project was launched under the Directorate of Livestock, Ministry of Fisheries and Livestock. Every appointment was given on contract basis and in the respective appointment letter it was categorically stated that after completion of the Project as per terms of the appointment letter and instrument of contract should be treated as the order of release. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">65.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the judgment of the High Court Division, we have found that the writ respondents were directed to regularize/absorb the writ petitioners under the revenue budget with continuity of service and other benefits subject to availability of the same/equivalent posts provided that the writ petitioners have requisite qualifications. While drawing such conclusion, the High Court Division relied upon the case of Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Labour and Manpower and others Vs. Mohammad Anisur Rahman and others reported in 18 MLR (AD) page 372.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">66.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the cited case this Division has observed, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Having considered the project pro-forma and other materials-on-record, the High Court Division found <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">that the Government made a clear promise</span> and commitment to transfer or absorb the writ petitioners in revenue budget. The High Court Division took into consideration that the Executive Committee of the National Economic Council (ECNEC) at its meeting dated 31.12.2007 had taken decision to <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">transfer all personnel of the development</span> project to the revenue budget and accordingly, all concerned were directed to take necessary steps to transfer all completed development project to the revenue set up. The High Court Division came to a finding that the conduct and the policy of the Government created legitimate expectation of the writ petitioners and such expectation has now become a vested and indefeasible right to be absorbed and regularized in the revenue budget. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">What is important to note here is that admittedly, the project started on 01.07.2001 and ended on 30.06.2009. Since the project started after 30.06.1997, the writ petitioners would not be automatically absorbed in the revenue budget. Though they have the legitimate expectation to be absorbed in the revenue budget such expectation can only be implemented subject to availability of the posts in the Bureau of Manpower Employment and Training (BMET).”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the cited case it was further observed,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>“In the light of the findings made before, we are inclined to dispose of the leave-petition with the following observations:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level3 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in list 117.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The leave petitioners are directed to absorb the writ petitioners-respondents under the revenue budget subject to availability of same/equivalent posts under the Bureau of Manpower Employment and Training provided that they have the requisite qualification.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level3 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in list 117.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the event of non availability of <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">adequate vacant posts to absorb the writ</span><span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> petitioners-respondents, the authority</span> shall not make any recruitment in BMET in future until the writ petitioners are absorbed provided that they have requisite qualification.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level3 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in list 117.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The writ petitioners-respondents are entitled to salaries and other benefits only for the period of rendition of their service.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">67.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the cited case it is not clear from the employment notification and other materials that whether the statutory provisions provided for selection process and appointment of the officers and employees as well as Government circular with subject heading, </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒDbœqb cªKí mgvwßi ci AZ¨vek¨Kxq c` evRvi ev‡R‡U ¯nvbvš—i</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> dated 24.12.2008 were complied with or not.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">68.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">When a person enters a temporary employment or gets engagement as a contractual employee and such engagement is not based on legally approved selection process as recognized by the rules or procedure, he is aware of the consequences of the appointment being temporary or contractual in nature. Such a person cannot invoke the theory of legitimate expectation for being regularized in the post when an appointment to the post could be made only by following the legally approved procedure for selection provided in the Rules quoted earlier. Since the recommendation of Public Service Commission is statutory requirement, before regularization of service, such recommendation must be accorded. The plea of legitimate expectation of the employees can not be raised which is contrary to statutory provisions. The legitimate expectation of an incumbent, if there be any, would not override the statutory provision to the contrary even if he continued in a temporary service by several orders of extension. The instant direction was given mainly on the ground of legitimate expectation of the writ petitioners inasmuch as we have already observed that the doctrine of legitimate expectation cannot override the statutory provision. Such doctrine would not have application where the legislature has enacted a statute. The theory cannot be pressed into service if its invocation would defeat or invalidate a legislation enacted by the legislature. It is not understandable as to how the service of the officers are to be regularized without recommendation of the Public Service Commission ignoring specific statutory provisions. That is, the High Court Division directed to regularize the service of the writ petitioners of this writ petition totally ignoring specific provisions provided in the statute as well as the circular dated 24.12.2008. The constitutional scheme which our country has adopted does not contemplete any back door appointment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">69.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have gone through the “Bidhimalas”, 1995 and 2005. Both the “Bidhimalas” were promulgated by the President of the Republic pursuant to the power conferred under article 133 of the Constitution in consultation with the Public Service Commission as per provision of article 140(2) of the Constitution. In wewagvjv, 2005 a non-obstante clause has been provided in Rule-3 stating that- </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ò3| wewagvjv cªvavb¨- AvcvZZt ejer Ab¨ †Kvb wewagvjv, Av‡`k ev wb‡`©‡k hvnv wKQyB _vKzK bv †Kb Dbœqb cªK‡íi Kg©KZ©v I Kg©Pvix‡`i †¶‡Î G wewagvjvi weavbejx Kvh©Kix nB‡e|Ó </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: TimesNewRoman;">In</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">wewagvjv, 2005 ÔDbœqb cªKíÕ</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">has been defined as</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒDbœqb cªKíÓ A_© 9 Gwcªj, 1972 Bs nB‡Z 30†k Ryb, 1997Bs ZvwiL ch©š— mg‡qi g‡a¨ ïi“nIqv miKvi Aby‡gvw`Z, Dbœqb ev‡RU cªKí mg~n</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">|</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> That is, by this definition development project has been used for limited purpose in respect of those Projects which were started on and from 09.04.1972 and ended on 30.06.1997. On perusal of the wewagvjv, 2005 it appears that by that “Bidhimala”, “Bidhimala” 1995 has not repealed expressly but overriding effect has been given using the aforesaid non-obstante clause. Maxwell on the interpretation of statues (Twelfth Edition) observed that a later statute may repeal an earlier one either expressly or by implication. But repeal by implication is not favourable to the Courts. If, as with all modern statutes, the later contains a list of earlier enactments which it expressly repeals, an omission of a particular statute from the list will be a strong indication of an intention not to repeal that statute. If, therefore, earlier and later statutes can reasonably be construed in such a way that both can be given effect to, this must be done. And when the later Act is worded in purely affirmative language, without any sort of negative expression or implied, it becomes even less likely that it was intended to repeal the earlier law. In the case of Municipal Council V. T.J. Joseph reported in AIR 1962 SC 922 it was observed that the legislature while enacting a law is aware of the existing laws of the same subject and hence if the legislature does not make a provision repealing the earlier law it does not indicate an intention to repeal the existing law. The “Bidhimala” 1995 is still in force.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">70.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">wewagvjv, 1995</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> we have found that the “deveopment project” has been defined as under: </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">2(K)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒDbœqb cªKíÓ A_© Dbœqb ev‡R‡U ev LvZfz³ †h mKj cªKí 1983 m‡bi ‡g gv‡mi 13 ZvwiL ev ZrcieZ©x Kv‡j ivR¯^ ev‡R‡U ¯nvbvš—wiZ nBqv‡Q ev nB‡e H mKj Dbœqb cªKí</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">|</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In both the “Bidhimalas” identical procedure of regularization of the service of the officers and employees from development project to revnue budget have been provided. In 1995, “Bidhimala” the same has been provided in Rule 3 with the heading</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒwbqwgZKiY c×wZ</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">and in Bidhi-4 of Bidhimala, 2005 with the heading</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒivR¯^ ev‡R‡U wbqwgZKiY c×wZ|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In both the Bidhimalas it has been provided that</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒivR ¯^ ev‡R‡U †Kvb c‡` mvgwqK fv‡e c`¯n †Kvb Kg©KZ©v I Kg©Pvix mswk−ó cªK‡í wb‡qvM miKv‡ii cªPwjZ wb‡qvM wewa ev wb‡qvM c×wZ ev mswk−ó cªK‡íi Rb¨ miKvi KZ©„K Aby‡gvw`Z wb‡qvM wewa AbymiY nB‡Z nB‡e|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">71.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the purpose of regularization of the service in the revenue budget from development project other legal requirements which have been provided in the “Bidhiamala” should be followed. Those are :</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(a)</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒD³ Kg©KZ©v ev Kg©Pvixi ivR¯^ ev‡R‡Ui c‡` wbqwgZKi‡Yi c~‡e©i PvKzixi avivevwnKZv _vwK‡Z nB‡e|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">and (b)</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">D³ Kg©KZ©v ev Kg©Pvixi ivR¯^ ev‡R‡Ui c‡` wbqwgZKi‡Yi c~‡e©i PvKzix m‡š—vlRbK nB‡Z nB‡e|</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">And another important precondition for regularization, which has been provided in both the “Bidhimalas” is:</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒKg© Kwgk‡bi AvIZvf~³ †Kvb c‡` Kwgk‡bi mycvwikμ‡g Ges Kwgk‡bi AvIZvewn©f~Z †Kvb c‡` wefvMxq c‡`vbœwZ ev evQvB KwgwUi mycvwikμ‡g wbqwgZ Kwi‡Z nB‡e|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;"> Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">That is, it is to be examined for regularising the service of an incumbent to revenue budget that he was appointed in the development project following the service Rules provided by the legislature; there must be continuity of service; service record in the development project must be satisfactory and the Public Service Commission must recommend in respect of the posts described in the schedule of the relevant law and, in other cases, must be recommended by departmental promotion committee or selection committee. Government cannot use its executive power to circumvent requirements of statutory rules. No body is entitled to flout the Rules. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">72.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">One thing is clear from the Rules that since the Rules provide the provisions of</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒwbqwgZKiY c×wZÓ Ò†R¨ôZv wba©viY</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">and</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">ÒcªK‡íi PvKzixKvj MYbv</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó, </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">of the employees who served in the project, it is apparent that the laws did not prohibit the provision of absorption and, thereafter, regularization of the officers and employees of the development project to revenue budget. It is entirely for the Government to take policy decision considering the facts, circumstances, viability and future necessity of the project subject matter whether or not to absorb the services of the project employees in the revenue set up. However, policy decision once taken should apply equaly and uniformly. Simultaneously, it is to be remembered that absorption of project employees, who obtained employment by taking recourse to back door method, is violative of the constitutional scheme as the appointments have to be made on merits of the candidates. Finally, such absorption and thereafter, regularization must be processed and done following the Government instructions as well as the statutory provisions as mentioned earlier.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">73.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is to be remembered that before regularization in the revenue budget in respect of the posts scheduled to be recruited by the Public Service Commission, recommendation of the Public Service Commission must be accorded. Similarly, recommendation of departmental promotion committee or selection committee is to be accorded for the posts which are not to be recruited by the Public Service Commission. That is, if the service of the officers and employees is transferred/absorbed in the revenue budget upon due compliance with the circular issued under Memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">bs-mg(mI e¨-4)-1c-1/2008-255 ZvwiLt 10†cŠl, 1415/24 wW‡m¤^i,200</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">8</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> then the service of the officers and employees of those transferred project should be regularized following the provisions of the applicable “Bidhimala” as quoted earlier. However, </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Òmgvß Dbœqb cªKí nB‡Z ivR¯^ ev‡R‡Ui c‡` wb‡qv‡Mi †¶‡Î eqm wkw_jKiY wewagvjv, 2005</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Ó</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> provides special privilege of relaxation of age limit of employees of development budget for participation for getting employment in the posts of revenue budget. That is, the legislature, considering the experience and disadvantageous position of the officers and employees of the Development Project, has provided such special privilege to them since they have lost their valuable times while serving in the Projects Since the provisions of “Bidhimalas” are statutory provisions the authority concerned must comply with the provisions of the </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ò</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bidhimalas</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ó</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> as quoted earlier before regularization of absorbed officers and employees in the revenue set up. However, this Court, is bound to insist the Government making regular and proper recruitments and is bound not to encourage or shut its eyes to the persistent transgression of the rules of regular recruitment. No court can direct the Government or its instrumentalities to regularize the service of the officers and employees of the development project in the revenue budget in the cases where statutory requirements have not been fulfilled. Regularization cannot be claimed as a matter of right. It is statutory requirement that opportunity shall be given to eligible persons by public notification and recruitment should be according to the valid procedure and appointment should be of the qualified persons found fit for appointment to a post or an office under the Government. When the High Court Division is approached for relief by filing writ petition, necessarily the High Court Division has to ask itself whether the person before it had any legal right to be enforced or not. It can not be directed to devise a third mode of selection.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">74.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, it is observed that:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The legitimate expectation would <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">not override the statutory provision.</span> The doctrine of legitimate expectation can not be invoked for creation of posts to facilitate absorption in the offices of the regular cadres/non cadres. Creation of permanent posts is a matter for the employer and the same is based on policy decision.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">While transferring any development</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> project and its manpower to revenue budget the provisions provided in the notifications, government orders and circulars quoted earlier must be followed. However, it is to be remembered that executive power can be exercised only to fill in the gaps and the same cannot and should not supplant the law, but only supplement the law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Before regularization of service of the officers and employees of the development project in the revenue budget the provisions of applicable “Bidhimala” must be complied with. Without exhausting the applicable provisions of the “Bidhimala” as quoted above no one is entitled to be regularised in the service of revenue budget since those are statutory provisions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The appointing authority, while regularising the officers and employees in the posts of revenue budget, must comply with the requirements of statutory rules in order to remove future complic-ation. The officers and employees of the development project shall get age relaxation for participation in selection process in any post of revenue budget as per applicable Rules.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">A mandamus can not be issued in favour of the employees directing the government and its instrumentalities to make anyone regularized in the permanent posts as of right. Any appointment in the posts described in the schedule of Bangladesh Civil Service Recruitment Rules, 1981, Gazetted Officers (Department of Live Stock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1984 and Non-gazetted Employees (Department of Live Stock Service) Recruitment Rules, 1985 bypassing Public Service Commission should be treated as back door appointment and such appointment should be stopped.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">To become a member of the service in a substantive capacity, appointment by the President of the Republic shall be preceded by selection by a direct recruitment by the PSC. The Government has to make appointment according to recruitment Rules by open competitive examination through the PSC.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Opportunity shall be given to eligible</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> persons by inviting applications through public notification and appointment should be made by regular recruitment through the prescribed agency following legally approved method consistent with the requirements of law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo4; tab-stops: list .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is not the role of the Courts to <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">encourage or approve appointments</span> made outside the constitutional scheme and statutory provisions. It is not proper for the Courts to direct absorption in permanent employment of those who have been recruited without following due process of selection as envisaged by the constitutional scheme.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">75.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the discussion made above and since it is not apparent from the judgment of the High Court Division and other materials available in the record that the procedure provided in the Government notification, circulars or orders and the process of appointment indicated in the “Bidhimalas” 1995 or 2005 have been followed duly for appointing the writ petitioners and that they are no longer in service in view of terms of appointment letters and contracts, the direction of the High Court Division to absorb/regularise their service giving continuity of the same can not be approved. So, the same is set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">76.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the light of the observation made above, the appeal and review petition are disposed of</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in; line-height: 115%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/Downloads/Issue__September__2019(2)/Issue__September_19__C.%20A.%20460%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">civil appeal no. 460 of 2017 with civil </span></strong></a><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">review petition no. 181 of 2018.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated 07.09.2016 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 7166 of 2015 and judgment and order dated 21.08.2017 passed by the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 1790 of 2017.)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
798	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Topcom Holdings Ltd. Vs.  Bangladesh &amp; ors.</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Admiralty Suit No. 29 of 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Saifur Rashid with  Ms. Zinia Amin, Advocates,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Topcom Holdings Limited </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; mso-yfti-tbllook: 480; mso-padding-alt: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">10.05.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/2012/September%202012/Issue%20__September__19(2)__Admiralty%20__29%20of%2018_Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Topcom Holdings Limited</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Government of Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .Respondents </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 19</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">08)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Order 39, Rule 1<u></u></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">After institution of the suit, when it would appear to the Court that if the temporary injunction is not granted, the suit itself may be infructuous or great hardship and prejudice may cause to the party, then, in order to keep the subject matter of the suit intact or for the purpose of preserving the rights of the parties, temporary injunction may be granted for a limited period or till the disposal of the suit. The cardinal principles for granting temporary injunction are that the applicant must satisfy the Court that (i) there is an arguable <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">prima facie</em> case, (ii) balance of inconvenience is in favour of the applicant and (iii) the applicant shall suffer irreparable loss and injury not commensurable in monetary terms unless the other party is restrained. It is a well-settled principle that granting or vacating the temporary injunction is a discretionary power of any Court, and a discretionary power is required to be exercised only in favour of those litigants who come before the Courts with clean hands. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>...(16 and 47)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Interpretation of Statute. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">What is lien:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">‘Lien’ is a right of retaining any property, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">goods and money against the service rendered</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> by any skilled/unskilled professional, or in exchange of or against the sale of any movable/immovable property. A lien is the right to retain property belonging to a debtor until he has discharged a debt due to the retainer of the property. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>...(25 and 29)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Interpretation of Statute.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">What is Maritime claim: </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">When a ‘common law lien’ is created in connection with the dealings of a vessel, it may give rise to a ‘maritime claim’. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                               </span>. . . (31)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Interpretation of Statute. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">What is Maritime lien:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A lien on a vessel, given to secure the claim of a creditor who provided maritime services to the vessel or who suffered an injury from the vessel’s use. -<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Also termed tacit hypothecation. </em>Although all ‘maritime liens’ are ‘maritime claims’, but all ‘maritime claims’ are not ‘maritime liens’. ‘Maritime lien’ is an important aspect of maritime law with the liability of contract that falls on ship and ships’ equipment. In other words, it is a privileged claim upon a ship for service rendered to, or injuries caused by the ship. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (33 and 36)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Words and Phrases </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Duties of an Advocate. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned members of the Bar that they, being the integral part of the Judiciary, should be more interested to dispose of the substantive matters pending before the Courts than showing their eagerness in obtaining the interim relief. Particularly, when any Court suggests that the substantive matter shall be heard on fast-track basis, the concerned Advocates should understand that while on the one side, the parties of the suit/case would get the aspired remedy, which would obviously include the interim relief, on the other, the Court would be able to reduce the number of backlog of cases. The learned Advocates should take into consideration the valuable time of the Courts that requires for adjudication upon the interim/interlocutory matters. Instead of compelling the Courts to spend time in dealing with interlocutory matters, if the learned Advocates extend their co-operation to dispose of the substantive matter, the Judiciary will be able, to some extent, to cope with the prevailing backlog. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . .(54)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Saifur Rashid with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ms. Zinia Amin, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .For the Plaintiff</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Syed Hasan Zubair, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .For the Defendant No. 2</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Ashadullah with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mst. Rohani Siddiqua, Advocates <u></u></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Defendant No. 5</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Nikhil Kumar Biswas</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For respondent No. 8.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 105%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">By</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;"> filing two separate applications, the defendant no. 2 (Director General of Food, Ministry of Food, Government of Bangladesh) and the defendant no. 5 (the PEC limited, an Indian Government entity) are praying to this Court for vacating the interim Order of Injunction passed by this Court on 28.06.2018, by which the defendant no. 2 has been restrained from making any payment to the defendant no. 3 (the Supreme Container Line, who chartered the Vessel MV RAINBOW FAIRY from the plaintiff of this suit). And, by filing another application the plaintiff is praying for temporary injunction against the defendant no. 2 restraining him to make any further payment to the defendant no. 5.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The background facts of filing these applications are that Topcom Holdings Limited, who is the disponent owner of the vessel M.V. RAINBOW FAIRY, as the plaintiff, filed the instant Admiralty Suit against the defendants for realization of its outstanding freight/hire under the time-charterparty dated 18.01.2018 for an amount of USD 274,677.98, equivalent to BDT 2,32,10,289.31. At the time of admission of the suit on 28.06.2018, the plaintiff also filed an application for temporary injunction restraining the defendant no. 2 from making any further payment of the outstanding amount of freight to the defendant no. 3 till disposal of the instant suit. After hearing the aforesaid application, the same was allowed. Now, the defendant nos. 2 &amp; 5 have come up with their respective applications for vacating the said Order of Injunction and the plaintiff has filed an application for modification of the Order dated 28.06.2018 to the effect that defendant nos. 2 &amp; 8 shall be restrained from making any payment to the defendant no. 5 (i.e. at the time of admission, Injunction Order was passed against the defendant no. 3, now the plaintiff prays for passing the same Order against the defendant no. 5, instead of the defendant no. 3).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Factual averments made by the respondent nos. 2 &amp; 5. </span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>In the applications filed by the defendant nos. 2 &amp; 5, it is stated, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia</em>, that under the Government to Government (G to G) negotiations, contract no. DGF/PEC-01 dated 25.10.2017 was signed between the DG, Food, Government of Bangladesh (defendant no. 2) and the PEC Limited, an enterprise of the Government of India (defendant no. 5) to purchase 100000 Metric Tons (mt) non-basmati parboiled rice from India; that<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>pursuant thereto, the Letter of Credit (L/C) No. 033017010569 was opened by the defendant no. 2 with Sonali Bank Limited (defendant no. 8) on 01.11.2017 in favour of the defendant no. 5; that Bill of Lading was signed for and on behalf of the vessel M. V. RAINBOW FAIRY; that the freight has been paid in advance; that as per the contract dated 25.10.2017 signed by the Bangladesh Government and the Indian exporter, the ship (the plaintiff) with the rice arrived at the Chittagong Port on 23.05.2018 and after completing the formalities with the customs and other authorities, offloading of rice started on 02.06.2018 and ended on 21.06.2018 and, thereafter, the vessel sailed out from the Chittagong Port on 25.06.2018. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;">It is further stated that the plaintiff did not submit the original copy of the charterparty or any certified copy thereof before this Court, the plaintiff has merely submitted a printed copy of the Form NYPE/93; that through the addendum no. 1, the plaintiff seeks to show that there is existence of the charterparty dated 18.01.2018, but it relates to a different vessel named M V ORCHID; that for the sake of argument, even if the said charterparty is taken to be for the vessel MV RAINBOW FAIRY, the said charterparty dated 18.01.2018 provides a “guarantee clause” of the performance of the defendant no. 3 and condition no. 6 of its addendum no. 1 provides that the disponent owner (the plaintiff) does not have any objections if the Supreme Container Line (defendant no. 3) receives freight payment on the basis of services performed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is further stated that although only 5% of the total L/C money amounting to USD 262,762 currently is due to be paid through the L/C opening Bank, but this Court’s Order has stopped further exports and imports between the Bangladesh Government and the said Indian Government’s enterprise; that the defendant no. 5 is not being allowed to enter into new business/contract with the Bangladesh Government; that due to the Order of Injunction passed by this Court, the defendant no. 5 is to pay 12% interest as per the Rules framed by the Central Bank of India; that the defendant no. 5 failed to supply 2,00,000 mts of rice to Bangladesh as the Indian Bank did not provide loan facility because of the fact that the previous loan has not yet been adjusted and, consequently, the defendant no. 5 has been bearing interest incurred thereon on top of losing new business; that they have sent e-Mail and letter by registered post to the address of the defendant no. 3 with a request to contest this suit so that they may be relieved of the hassle they are facing in dealing with this suit owing to the alleged fault of the defendant no. 3, but till date they have not heard anything from the defendant no. 3.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Factual statements of the plaintiff:</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>In the Written Objection filed by the plaintiff, it is stated that although the Fixture Note dated 18.01.2018 mentions the name of MV ORCHID as the performing vessel, however, the addendum no. 4 dated 19.04.2018 clearly shows that the above-named MV ORCHID was replaced by the plaintiff-vessel MV RAINBOW FAIRY as the performing vessel; that the plaintiff has<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>not been paid off its freight by the defendant no. 3; that the claim of the plaintiff requires to be either admitted or denied by the defendant no. 3 who is yet to appear before this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Submissions advanced and the arguments made by the learned Advocates for the respondent nos. 2 &amp; 5:</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Placing the provisions of Section 5(1)(a) of the Admiralty Court Act, 2000 (shortly, the Admiralty Court Act) before this Court and, side by side, taking me through the Fixture Note and the Four Addenda thereto, the learned Advocate for the defendant no. 2, Mr. Md Syed Hasan Zubair and the learned Advocate for the defendant no. 5, Mr. Ashadullah, at the very outset submit that the factual contentions of these two defendants being the same, their submissions may be recorded as joint submissions. They, thus, jointly submit that in the light of the fact that Fixture Note with the four addenda were executed in India between the plaintiff and the defendant no. 3 and since the main grievance and allegation is only against the defendant no. 3 and, further, given the fact that the place of business of the defendant no. 3 is in Mumbai, India, the jurisdiction of the suit falls outside Bangladesh territory as per Section 5(1)(a) </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">[<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">aviv 5(1)(K)]</strong> </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;">of the Admiralty Court Act. They strenuously submit that the charterparty having been executed outside Bangladesh territory between two foreign parties, namely, the plaintiff and the defendant no. 3, and the other defendants of the suit admittedly being not party to the said charterparty, they were illegally made defendants to the suit by the plaintiff with a motive to make them scapegoat, so that the defendant nos. 2 &amp; 5 become compelled to contact the defendant no. 3 towards ensuring the presence of the defendant no. 3 before this Court. They submit that since the defendant no. 5 has paid off the freight in advance to the defendant no. 3, the outstanding 5% L/C money lying with the defendant no. 2 is the payment against the rice purchased by the defendant no. 2 from the defendant no. 5. They argue that had it been the scenario that the defendant no. 5 would pay the freight to the defendant no. 3 out of this 5% outstanding L/C money, the plaintiff would have been justified to seek Order of Restraint upon the outstanding 5% money. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">They submit that since it is evident that the Form NYPE/93, which has been produced before this Court, was not executed by the aforesaid parties to the contract, it is not a contract at all and, thus, not binding upon the defendants of the suit. They further submit that, even for the sake of argument if the template of the Form NYPE/93 is taken to be a valid one, since the Clause No. 40 of the said prescribed Form NYPE/93 provides for arbitration in case of any dispute arising out of the said contract, the plaintiff is required to approach the arbitration forum and, hence, the present suit is not maintainable. They next submit that the contract was signed between Bangladesh and India for export and import of rice, which is the commercial dealing between Bangladesh and India, and the Order of Injunction in fact restrained the performance of international contractual obligations arising out of international trade. They submit that the Order of Injunction virtually stopped the payment of L/C money relating to international trade and non-payment of L/C money may cause serious repercussions on the international trade of the country inasmuch as payment of the L/C money cannot be stopped by way of injunction as per the provisions of various International Banking and Trading Laws, such as UCP-600, UCC, URC-522 and ISBP (International Standard Banking Practice). </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">They submit that the ‘maritime lien’ contemplates against ship/vessel; not against the freight or damages and, that is why, ‘maritime lien’ compels the ship for payment of a claim founded upon the maritime law when a judicial proceeding is taken under the Admiralty Court Act against the vessel. He submits that since the vessel M V RAINBOW FAIRY left the Chittagong Port on 25.06.2018 after discharging the rice as per the Bill of Lading, and since the plaintiff filed the suit for charges and damages asserting the same as the ‘maritime lien’, institution of the suit for money decree in the name of the Admiralty Suit is a fraud upon the statute, as apparently the present suit is cunningly filed for avoiding Court fees of a significant amount of money which would have required for institution of a Money Suit. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Submissions made by the learned Advocate for the plaintiff: </span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>On the other hand, the learned Advocate for the plaintiff places Section 3(2)(h) </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">[aviv 3(2)(R)] </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">of the Admiralty Court Act and submits that since the plaintiff’s claim has arisen out of hire of its ship, the Admiralty Court is the proper forum for adjudication upon the claim of the plaintiff. Then Mr. Saifur Rashid refers to Clause 23 of the Form NYPE/93 and submits that as per Clause 23 of the aforesaid Form NYPE/93, the plaintiff has a lien on all sub-freights and sub-hires of the vessel M V RAINBOW FAIRY, if the freight of the vessel is not paid in due time, and since the plaintiff did not receive its freight in time in spite of sending repeated reminders to the defendants, the plaintiff has the right to exercise lien upon sub-freight. In support of his submissions, he refers to the case of Care Shipping Corporation Vs Latin American Shipping Corporation reported in (1983) 1 All ER 1121 and the case of Mareva Compania Naviera SA Vs International Bulk Carriers SA reported in (1975) Vol 2 Lloyd’s Rep 509, CA.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;">He next submits that Form NYPE/93 is a standard Form for using it as the charterparty. He, in an effort to place before this Court the nitty-gritty of the Form NYPE/93, goes on to contend that NYPE stands for the “New York Produce Exchange” and the Association of Ship Brokers and agents of USA Inc has been issuing the said Form since 06.11.1913 and because of the fact that the same was issued for the last time on 14<sup>th</sup> September 1993, it is known in the maritime world as “NYPE/93”. Mr. Saifur Rashid submits that although a template of the Form NYPE/93 has been filed before this Court without producing the signed copy of the charterparty, but since it is being used by all the stakeholders of the maritime industry, including the Baltic and International Maritime Council (BIMCO) and the Federation of National Associations of Ship Brokers and Agents (FONASBA), the plaintiff and its charterers/sub-charterer have also used the template of Form NYPE/93 as the charterparty.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;">He lastly submits that since the plaintiff has not received the freight payment from the defendant no. 3, the defendant no. 5’s claim of making advance freight payment to the defendant no. 3 requires to be proved by way of adducing evidence and, therefore, presence of all these defendants are necessary for an effective and fair adjudication of the suit. He submits that if the money is released from the lien, this suit shall be infructuous and therefore, the facts and circumstances of the case fairly demand that an Order of Temporary Injunction should be passed against the Sonali Bank, Foreign Exchange Branch the L/C opening Bank<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>(defendant no. 8) and the Directorate General of Food (the defendant no. 2) restraining them from making payment of the outstanding 5% L/C amount to the defendant no. 5 (PEC Limited), till the plaintiff’s outstanding amount is cleared off or till disposal of the suit and, also, the two applications, filed by the defendant nos. 2 and 5 for vacating the Order of Injunction dated 28.06.2018 be rejected, otherwise, the plaintiff shall be seriously prejudiced and shall suffer irreparable loss and injury. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Upon hearing the learned Advocates for both the sides and perusal of the relevant laws, it appears to this Court that since these applications are regarding granting or vacating temporary injunction, it would be useful if it be learnt as to under what legal provisions as well as under what factual circumstances a Court grants temporary injunction and when it may be vacated/varied/ modified. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 6 of the Admiralty Court Act and Rule 3 of the Admiralty Rules, 1912 (Admiralty Rules) make it mandatory for the litigants to comply with the provisions of the Code of the Civil Procedure, 1908 (CPC) in drawing up, subscribing and verifying a plaint and Rule 35 of the Admiralty Rules mandates this Court to resort to the CPC for execution of a decree.
