text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iii) </span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The defendant no. 5 shall either furnish a Bank Guarantee of the equivalent amount of the money (i.e. the amount of money which is going to be released now) to this Court or in the alternative, the defendant no. 5 shall execute a bond in favour of the defendant no. 2 confirming that in course of completing the exportation of the rest of the quantity of rice to the defendant no. 2, the latter shall be competent to retain the equivalent amount of money at any point of time to satisfy any Order or decree passed by this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iv)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the defendant no. 5 is directed to remain present in this Court without fail whenever this suit would appear in the ‘Cause List’ so that the suit may be expeditiously disposed of.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(v)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned Advocate shall ensure the presence of any relevant witness of the defendant no. 5, if this Court intends to take his/her deposition as a Court Witness (C/W). In the event of failure to comply with this condition by the learned Advocate for the respondent no. 5, he shall be liable to furnish a written explanation before this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">51.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the result, the applications filed by the defendant nos. 2 &amp; 5 are allowed and the Order of interim injunction passed by this Court on 28.06.2018 restraining the defendant no. 2 from making any payment to the defendant no. 3 is vacated. Further, the application filed by the plaintiff praying for restraining the defendant nos. 2 &amp; 8 from making further payment to the defendant no. 5 is rejected. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">52.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">If the defendant no. 5 wishes to file any Written Statement in this suit, he is directed to file it within 7 (seven) days from the date of receipt of this Judgment and Order. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">53.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The suit is fixed for framing issues on 22.05.2019. Let the matter appear in the list under the heading for ‘Framing Issue’ on 22.05.2019. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">54.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Before parting with this Judgment and Order, I find it pertinent to remind the learned members of the Bar that they, being the integral part of the Judiciary, should be more interested to dispose of the substantive matters pending before the Courts than showing their eagerness in obtaining the interim relief. Particularly, when any Court suggests that the substantive matter shall be heard on fast-track basis, the concerned Advocates should understand that while on the one side, the parties of the suit/case would get the aspired remedy, which would obviously include the interim relief, on the other, the Court would be able to reduce the number of backlog of cases. The learned Advocates should take into consideration the valuable time of the Courts that requires for adjudication upon the interim/interlocutory matters. Instead of compelling the Courts to spend time in dealing with interlocutory matters, if the learned Advocates extend their co-operation to dispose of the substantive matter, the Judiciary will be able, to some extent, to cope with the prevailing backlog. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">55.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In this suit, after hearing the learned Advocate for the defendant no.5 on his application for vacating the Order of injunction, this Court had suggested that the suit shall be heard on priority basis by fixing the next date for framing issues. It was observed by this Court that if it surfaces upon examining the oral and documentary evidence that the suit is not maintainable against the defendant no. 5, then the suit would be proceeded only against the defendant no. 3. Had the learned Advocate conceded to the above suggestion of this Court, the defendant no.5 could have been permanently relieved of the hassle he is facing and on the other hand, this Court could have disposed of a substantive matter with the amount of time that required for disposing of these interim applications. Now, by getting the aspired relief in these applications, although the defendant no.5’s L/C money would be released subject to depositing the equivalent amount of security, he remains entangled with the suit.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/2012/September%202012/Issue%20__September__19(2)__Admiralty%20__29%20of%2018_Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__3.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Admiralty Suit No. 29 of 2018</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
